Introduction

Assignment08, for me, was an iteration of the previous assignments, by design, as discussed throughout the Introduction to Program= ming Python course. The following is a recap of how I used previous assignme= nts to guide my decision making for Assignment08 while incorporating lessons from = Week 8. Below I will provide work from the past four weeks of the class to illustrate differences and similarities in coding which provides a foundati= on for learning in order to complete Assignment08.

 

Lessons Learned from Previous Assignments

Table 1, below, shows the progression of learning I un= derwent throughout the past four weeks for the sake of brevity. Ive selected onl= y of few of the elements of the assignments that focus on the interactions with = the users as well as the interaction between the programmers and different type= s of files.

 

Table 1 Progression example of the assignments of Assignment05, Assignemnt06, and Assignment07

Menu

The menu allows users to interact with the program and= a gateway to the rest of the program. When building the menu and applying to the assignments, I did not feel the need to change the code, Figure 1, below, a= s it served the purpose of the assignment, easy to read not only for users but f= or future programmers as well. Although I opted out of using a menu in Assignment07, the concept remains consistent, provide the user a string of = text that indicates the user has a choice in actions that the program would perf= orm.

 

Figure 1 Consistent menu code throughout the assignme= nts.

Inputs from Users

Students learned about the input(<= /span>) method in order to provide some sort of interaction with the user as well a= cquiring the knowledge to capture, store, and retrieve data. One input() method was an opportunity to ask the user which action the user wanted to t= ake from the menu. Dependent on the assignment, the options would be placed in a while loop that when an if or elif statement we= re met would perform an action. The other input() metho= d used consistently throughout the assignments asked the user to enter a string of text that would be captured for f= urther use within the program, stored, or retrieved through text input. All had the same type of input, but the lessons usage varied. As youll see in Table = 1, above, I did not change the method of capturing input from the user. In Ass= ignment05, I wanted to ensure that users were able to easily read the data and had qui= te a few print statements in my main body which makes it look messy, whereas in Assignment06 its cleaned up as we were taught about methods and better o= rganizing our code. Assignment07, for ease I grouped the append(<= /span>) method with the inputs, which I still struggle with as I feel it process the data and should be been placed in the Processor class, but it worked and at= the point of creating the working program thats all that mattered.

 

Saving to a File

Each assignments challenge was to save the user input = into a file, each had differing means of doing so. Saving to a file requires using= an open() and close() method in the program and learning = about the different modes when opening the file. Similar to the Inputs from Users code, we see that in Table 1, above, the code becomes more complicated, but less messy. Less print statements and better organization of data as well as more precise and useful comments. Difficulties I have to overcome is knowin= g to proper code that will work rather than testing out code I hope will w= ork. It will be something I assume I will struggle with this issue as I continue to learn more complicated programming as the class lecturer, Randal Root, emphasizes= in the class.

 

Reading from a File

Table 1, above, illustrates the progression of learnin= g that requires, again, an easier to follow code with increasingly complicated act= ions. Assignment05 is heavy with print() functions, and while code from both Assignment06 and Assignment07 have close to same numbe= r of lines as Assignment05, they are still easier to read as and communicate wit= h classes and methods within the program.

 

Implementing Lessons in Assignment08

Continuing with the theme of building upon a foundatio= n of learning, I used a lot of the script from previous assignments to provide t= he structure for Assignment08. Our learning was expanded in this section by learning about classes and its elements. Assignment08s task was to build= a list that prompts user to add a product and its price using the Product class co= de provided by Mr. Root. The challenge was not in developing the code but in writing the code properly in order to interact with the provided starter co= de. Below I will showcase how used previous lessons to build that foundation.

 

Menu

I maintained the menu, Figure 2, format because it is a reminder that If it aint broke, dont f= ix it. Yes, it is a simple method and the format isnt exactly pretty, but it is easy= to read and select from, there was no need to change it.

 

Figure 2 Menu for Assignment08, where I maintained the same format as previous assignments.

 

Inputs from Users

In an effort not to complicate matters by adding more methods to the IO class or the FileProcessor cl= ass, which is a lessoned from assignments past, I included an appe= nd() method in the method to prompt users for input which I called add_product_data, Figure 3. I called the Product clas= s, (user_product_name and user_produ= ct_price), and put it into an object called product, converted the object into a string using the to_string method from the Product cla= ss. All of which I feel should be in the FileProcessor class. In order to become more proficient in organizing my code Id like = to include the append in the Processor class, but am not comfortable quite yet. This, = input method was the most challenging, as Im sure was the intention, which wou= ld be how students would incorporate this weeks lesson into the program. I my struggle was at its peak when I tried to call the errors in the Product cla= ss but, because I did not include the Product class into an object, was not reachable. It clicked when I followed the book, Chapter 8, Python Programming for the Absolute Beginner, Third Edition, by Michael Dawson= s Critter program did it really click.

 

Figure 3 add_product_data method where I include the append method

Saving to a File

For Assignment08, saving data to a file is similar to = past assignments and I used the open method to open the file and used the w= (write) mode to open the file if it did not exist and to overwrite data from the fi= le. I use the write mode to because it is the easiest concept for me to grasp when coding to it. In the future I would like to practice with a (append).=

 

Figure 4 save_to_data_file method with w (write) mode.

Reading from a File

The concept of reading from a file method was the easi= est to grasp as it was a similar format to the previous assignments except this ti= me this time I understood the lst_of_product_objects.append(line) was a string and it was not necessary to create another object into and nes= t it into the lst_of_product_objects.append() method= .

 

Figure 5 read_data_from_file method using the lst_of_product_objects.a= ppend() method to pull data from the file.

 

Summary

The Introduction to Programming Python course is a= means for students to learn about programming through progressive learning techni= ques that build upon knowledge every week. I confirm the success of this techniq= ue by applying it to build my Assignment08 above as I have not only demonstrat= ed growth of knowledge but in its application.
